導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念：查核表 = 知識差距分析工具

附錄一的查核表不只是「收文清單」，更是技術轉移啟動時最重要的差距分析（Gap Analysis）工具。正確使用方式是在技術轉移啟動後立即填寫，為每一項目標記：

  • Available（已備齊）：文件完整，可直接移交
  • Partial（部分具備）：文件存在但不完整，需補充
  • Missing（缺失）：文件尚未建立，需要重新產生

這份差距分析的輸出直接驅動風險登錄冊（Risk Register）的建立——「Missing」項目通常就是高風險項目，需要立即分配資源處理。

比喻說明：搬家前的庫存清點

想像你要把一間運轉中的廚房（原廠）搬到另一個地方（接收廠）繼續營業。這張查核表就像是「搬家前的廚房庫存清點表」：鍋子、食譜、食材供應商聯絡方式、健康許可證……每一樣都要逐一確認是否帶走。少了任何一項，新廚房就無法在第一天正常開門。

大分子（生物製劑）多了「細胞株來源（Cell Bank）」這一行——這就像廚房獨門配方的「酵母菌種」，沒有它，整個生產就無從開始。

重點提示：大分子 vs. 小分子的關鍵差異

仔細比對查核表，大分子（生物製劑）專屬項目揭示了生物製劑TT的核心複雜性：

  • Cell Bank / Origin of Cell Bank：MCB（主要細胞庫）與WCB（工作細胞庫）的特性描述文件，是生物製劑製程的起點
  • Control Strategy：大分子列為必要，小分子未標記——因生物製劑的製程複雜度使控制策略成為TT成敗關鍵
  • Waste/Vent Characterization：生物製劑廢棄物（含活性生物物質）需特別處理，小分子則無此強制要求

小分子則多了物理化學特性：粒徑（Particle Size）、多形體（Polymorphs）、溶解度（Solubility）、毒理數據（Toxicology）、生體可用率（Bioavailability）——這些是固態製劑和化學合成製程特有的考量。

CDMO實務應用：簽約前必備清單

作為CDMO，在與生物製劑客戶簽署技術轉移協議前，以下文件屬於「不可或缺（Non-negotiable）」：

  • Cell Bank Origin Documentation（細胞株起源文件）
  • Process Description + CPPs with ranges（含參數範圍的製程描述）
  • Current Specifications & CQAs（現行規格與關鍵品質屬性）
  • 至少3批歷史批次數據（Historical Batch Data）
  • Stability Data（穩定性數據，至少初步結果）

若客戶無法提供上述文件，CDMO應在合約中明確界定「客戶責任（Client Obligation）」並連結時程里程碑，避免因文件缺失造成TT延誤而引發商業糾紛。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 若客戶無法提供「Development Run Data」，這對你的工程批（Engineering Run）規劃有何影響？你會如何在風險登錄冊中記錄此差距？
  2. 「Control Strategy」僅在大分子欄位標記 x，但小分子是否也應有控制策略？查核表的設計邏輯是什麼？
  3. 「Extractable/Leachable/Adsorption Data」在大小分子都標記，但生物製劑為何對此項更敏感？請從產品CQA角度分析。
附錄二 (Appendix 2) — 生物製劑案例研究 Section 9.1–9.2：摘要與主要挑戰

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer

9   Appendix 2 – Case Studies: Biologics

9.1   Summary

This chapter presents case studies that illustrate key technology transfer concepts presented in this Guide, with an emphasis on utilizing CMOs.

The key components of any technology transfer are the technical challenges and effective program management. With any technology transfer program, technical challenges can arise that could subsequently impact the planned timelines, process performance, and product quality. These challenges should be addressed in a collaborative way between the sending and receiving units to minimize delays in the program and frustrations arising between sites.

In this chapter, five case studies are presented, the first two from a client perspective and the subsequent three from a CMO perspective. These examples demonstrate a range of challenges which occurred during technology transfer programs and how they were subsequently resolved.

The molecules in these case studies are primarily monoclonal antibodies (mAbs) but the lessons learned are generally applicable across all molecular classes. Manufacturing processes for mAbs have become relatively well-defined and are often based on platform technologies that can be effectively leveraged; there is a generally broad knowledge base. In addition, the advent of single-use technologies is facilitating transfers by minimizing changes in equipment and operating parameters.

The amount of drug substance manufacturing experience that smaller companies typically have is modest, often at different scales and with limited development history and process knowledge. Transfers represent the opportunity to right-size a process and implement process improvements with an eye to minimizing changes that might impact product comparability. Technology transfers also potentially offer an opportunity to assess new technologies, such as continuous manufacturing and PAT, if the CMO has these capabilities.

9.2   Main Challenges

One of the main challenges for successful technology transfer utilizing a contract manufacturer is selecting the right CMO and developing a good partnership. From an operational perspective, this involves ensuring capacity (i.e., having manufacturing slots available within an acceptable time frame) and ensuring appropriate process and analytical capabilities necessary for project success. Demand for manufacturing slots will vary over time, but demand for capacity continues to grow and is a potential constraint that is a priority planning consideration. Recent experience with these case studies has resulted in successful transfers (i.e., completion of first GMP batch in approximately 12 months).

Another main challenge for a small to mid-size company executing technology transfer is how to deal with a lack of development history or process knowledge, either due to limited manufacturing experience or insufficient process development. Performing a gap assessment prior to initiating the transfer and then sharing this assessment with the CMO at initiation (to gain alignment and ensure transparency) can be critical for success. Early involvement of manufacturing teams during technology transfer and development phases is also critical for successful implementation of the process at scale.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念：為何以mAb為主角？

本附錄選擇單株抗體（mAb）作為主要案例，原因有三：

  • 市場主流：mAb佔全球生物製劑市值超過一半，CDMO最常遇到此類品項
  • 平台製程成熟：CHO細胞培養 → 蛋白A親和層析 → 病毒去活化 → 精製層析的平台路徑已建立，CDMO可快速評估接收可行性
  • 一次性技術普及：Single-use bioreactor/filtration等技術大幅降低了設備配置差異，減少TT中的設備兼容性風險

mAb的經驗雖可類推至其他生物製劑，但融合蛋白（fusion proteins）、ADC（抗體藥物結合物）、細胞基因治療（CGT）等分子則有各自獨特的挑戰，不能完全套用。

重點提示：「12個月完成第一批GMP批」的含義

文中提到成功TT的基準是「約12個月內完成第一批GMP批次」。這個數字代表從CMO選定到GMP生產完成。對CDMO業務開發而言，這是客戶最常問的問題之一。

影響這12個月的關鍵因素：

  • 文件完整性（缺文件 = 延誤最大來源）
  • 長前置期物料（如一次性袋組、層析介質、細胞培養基）的採購時間
  • CDMO的製程工程師是否熟悉客戶的平台製程
  • 監管策略（工程批是否需要ICH Q5E可比性研究）

比喻說明：小公司TT困境

小到中型生物技術公司常面臨的情況：臨床前/Phase I期的製程是由學術實驗室或小型CRO完成，批量小（1–10L）、記錄不完整，現在要轉移到2,000L商業規模。

這就像一位廚師在家裡用小鍋試驗出一道菜，現在要複製給工廠大量生產——不僅食譜要完整，還要考慮熱傳導、混合效率、原料批次差異……原先在小鍋裡自然成立的條件，大鍋裡可能完全失效。

這就是為什麼「gap assessment前置」如此重要：早點發現差距，才能在合約中明確定義誰來填補、費用如何分攤。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 文中提到「capacity continues to grow」是指需求持續增加。從CDMO角度，產能不足對客戶TT時程有何影響？你會如何在提案階段管理客戶期望？
  2. 「gap assessment prior to initiating the transfer」與「gap assessment during transfer」有何不同？分別在哪個情境下使用？
Section 9.3 — 技術轉移階段概覽 (Overview of Technology Transfer Phases)

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer

9.3   Overview of Technology Transfer Phases

As described in Chapter 3, there are six phases of technology transfer:

  1. Project Initiation: Form technology transfer team and develop charter
  2. Knowledge Transfer: Consolidate knowledge for transfer and agree on high level technology transfer proposal
  3. Project Delivery Planning: Identify risks, conduct risk assessments, and develop technology transfer plan
  4. Operational Readiness
  5. Project Implementation: Process (procedure) qualification
  6. Project Close-Out: Finalize technology transfer and perform review

The approach presented in this chapter takes a modified approach that has been successfully utilized by small to mid-sized companies. The three general stages, as defined in this chapter from the client perspective, are:

  1. CMO Selection
  2. Project Initiation
  3. Project Execution

In relation to the six phases presented in Chapter 3: CMO selection precedes establishment of a technology transfer team but is a necessary precursor for outsourcing.

  • Project initiation incorporates aspects of phases 1 to 3.
  • Project execution includes aspects of phase 3 as well as phases 4 and 5. Phase 6 can range in scope from completion of a pilot or engineering batch to submission of a regulatory filing as well as a lessons learned exercise between the client and the CMO.

From the CMO's perspective, stage gates can be defined within the detailed project plan per their procedures to ensure that activities (such as document transfer, preparation of GMP documentation, etc.) occur in a timely manner to support manufacture. This is also a good example of the need for a small to mid-sized company to have flexible and adaptable operational and quality systems. Typically, they will not have formal technology transfer procedures and it will be advantageous and efficient to utilize and leverage the CMO's procedures, recognizing that these will likely differ between different CMOs.

Figure 9.1: Example Technology Transfer Process Flow
(Used with permission from Patheon, part of Thermo Fisher Scientific)

9.3.1   CMO Selection

The CMO selection process is initiated by developing a list of candidates based on industry knowledge and experience that meet baseline criteria, including scale, capability, and compliance history. A detailed Request for Proposal (RFP) should be developed that includes an appropriate amount of process detail, analytical method descriptions, the product specification, a bill of materials, and requests for any development work. Target dates for major deliverables should also be included, such as any requirements to have toxicology or clinical studies initiated by a certain date or if there are any commitments to achieve a target date for an investigational new drug filing.

Adequate process detail is necessary to ensure that the proposals that are received in response to the RFP are comparable and permit an appropriate comparison. It is also important to initiate the CMO selection process with adequate time for refining responses to the RFP. In general, there might be at least one to two cycles of proposal refinement that will allow an accurate comparison between CMOs and facilitate contract negotiation. In addition, an appropriately detailed RFP permits the CMO to properly assess their ability to run the process and be successful within project timeline expectations.

For example, an RFP can be structured as follows:

  • 1 Introduction — Background, Objectives, Response to RFP
  • 2 Scope of Services Requested — Technology Transfer, Analytical Services, Engineering and Clinical Batches, PPQ Batches, Process Validation, Stability, Additional Services
  • 3 Supporting Information — development reports, batch records (if available), PFDs, specifications, test methods, bill of materials, etc.

For the first case study, this approach started with engagement of six candidate CMOs. The proposals received were reviewed and a head to head analysis was performed on work scope, cost, and timing. From this assessment, two lead candidates were identified and due diligence audits were performed, resulting in a lead and a backup CMO.

9.3.2   Project Initiation

Once the CMO is selected, contract and quality agreement negotiations are immediately initiated, utilizing CMO templates for efficiency. A project kickoff meeting should be scheduled as soon as possible at the CMO and is critical for establishing the personal connections and lines of communication.

The composition of the client project team may vary, but will typically include a project leader, project manager, process and analytical SMEs, a CMC regulatory representative, and a quality representative. The CMO project team will be comparable and complementary.

Establishment of personal connections between these team members and their counterparts at the CMO are invaluable in anticipation that there will be challenges during the technology transfer and manufacturing that will require good working relationships to ensure appropriate and timely resolution. Face-to-face meetings are critical for establishing relationships and lines of communication.

9.3.3   Project Execution

The third aspect of project initiation is document transfer and sharing of the QTPP, CQAs, and CPPs that define the control strategy. These documents are important because they:

  • Define the intended use and product quality profile
  • Ensure that technology transfer process development/optimization begins with the end in mind and that client and CMO goals and expectations are aligned
  • Define those product characteristics or CQAs that must be monitored and controlled during technology transfer

Project execution follows a standard course of events. The following is an overview of activities undertaken in both case studies:

  • Process assessment and identification of the need for process development/optimization for facility fit
  • Identification and immediate ordering of long lead time materials/consumables
  • Small scale/development studies, as appropriate
  • Method transfer and qualification, as appropriate
  • Development of GMP documentation, including batch records, test methods, specification, etc.
  • Pilot scale run, if needed
  • Engineering run, if needed
  • GMP run(s)
  • Analytical comparability
  • Regulatory submission

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念：三階段 vs. 六階段框架的調和

本節將ISPE六階段框架（教科書模型）與小型生技公司實際使用的三階段模型（實務模型）對應起來：

  • CMO Selection（遴選）→ 先於Phase 1，是外包的前提
  • Project Initiation（啟動）→ 涵蓋Phases 1–3（組隊、知識整合、風險識別）
  • Project Execution（執行）→ 涵蓋Phases 3–5（OQ、PQ、PPQ）

這種「壓縮框架」在小公司常見，因為沒有足夠的專職TT人員執行完整六階段的儀式性流程。CDMO必須理解客戶可能沒有正式的TT SOP，並主動以自身程序引導流程。

RFP結構框架：CDMO收到的標準投標書

RFP架構（客戶發出，CDMO回應）
├── 1. Introduction
│   ├── Background（產品背景）
│   ├── Objectives（目標，如首批GMP日期）
│   └── Response Instructions（回覆規格）
│
├── 2. Scope of Services
│   ├── Technology Transfer（文件接收、製程轉移）
│   ├── Analytical Services（方法轉移、QC建立）
│   ├── Engineering / Clinical Batches
│   ├── PPQ Batches（通常3批）
│   ├── Process Validation
│   ├── Stability（方案設計、樣品存放）
│   └── Additional Services（法規支援、原料採購）
│
└── 3. Supporting Information
    ├── Development Reports
    ├── Batch Records（若有）
    ├── PFDs + Specifications
    ├── Analytical Methods
    └── Bill of Materials

重點提示：Stage Gates的作用

Stage Gate（階段關卡）是CDMO保護自身和客戶的機制——只有前一個里程碑確認完成，才允許進入下一階段。例如：

  • 文件傳輸 Gate：文件收齊並審核通過 → 才開始編寫批次記錄
  • 方法轉移 Gate：分析方法資格確認 → 才開始工程批
  • 工程批 Gate：製程數據審查通過 → 才進入GMP批

Stage Gate能早期發現問題，避免在昂貴的GMP批才發現分析方法根本無法用於接收廠設備。

比喻說明：面對面會議為何不可省略？

文中特別強調「Face-to-face meetings are critical」。在視訊會議盛行的時代，這個建議仍然成立，原因是：技術轉移過程中不可避免地會出現問題（偏差、批次失敗、客戶投訴）。

這就像急診室的醫護團隊——平常你可以用電話溝通，但在緊急情況下，面對面的默契、信任感與即時決策速度是電話無法取代的。TT啟動會議就是在「真正的危機還沒來之前」，先建立這種信任基礎。

CDMO實務應用：Long Lead Time物料管理

「Identification and immediate ordering of long lead time materials/consumables」是執行階段的第二個行動項目，時序上比多數人預期的要早。

生物製劑TT中常見的長前置期物料：

  • 蛋白A層析介質（MabSelect Resin）：前置期6–12週
  • 一次性生物反應器袋組（SU Bioreactor Bag）：8–16週
  • 細胞培養基（Basal + Feed Media）：如為客製配方可達12週
  • 病毒過濾器（Virus Filter）：6–10週

若啟動會議後才開始詢價採購，這些物料的到位時間很可能成為工程批的瓶頸。最佳實務是在RFP階段即要求客戶提供BOM，CDMO收到後立即評估哪些屬於長前置期物料。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 若CDMO同時收到6家客戶的RFP，如何快速評估哪些客戶的製程具備轉移可行性？你會看哪三個指標？
  2. 「1–2 cycles of proposal refinement」代表客戶與CDMO在合約前會有多次溝通。從CDMO角度，哪些資訊最容易在第一輪RFP中被遺漏，需要在第二輪補充？
Section 9.4 — 風險管理 (Risk Management)

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer

9.4   Risk Management

Although there is a defined process for CMO selection that plays a key role in reducing risk, no formal risk assessment (technical, operational, or business) was performed by the client for initiating technology transfer in these case studies. Client SME experience working with CMOs and due diligence audits were used to informally assess risk. However, formal risk assessments are performed by the client as part of change control and are subsequently formally introduced through collaboratively performed FMEAs as the project advances toward pivotal study or PPQ.

The requirements of the selection process that reduce risk are as follows:

  • Commercial experience
  • Appropriate scale (current and future)
  • Capacity (availability of manufacturing slots)
  • Demonstrated ability to expand capacity/capabilities
  • Compliance history
  • Technical skill/experience

These requirements were met through the selection process that included a combination of the following:

  • Proposal submission based on the detailed RFP
  • Site visit
  • Due diligence audit
  • Professional experience
"This could generally be considered a standard practice for small companies."

A key component of the proposal is an adequately detailed project plan that is utilized by both client and CMO project managers to manage timelines and inherently manage risk associated with those activities by identifying critical path activities. Capacity and technical experience play important roles in meeting deadlines and ensuring that the ultimate goal of the technology transfer, production of the first GMP batch, is successful and on time.

Once a contract is signed, the project is initiated with a face-to-face team meeting at the CMO. The purpose of this meeting is to formally present the project goals and objectives and initiate relationships between SMEs and other project team members. Document transfer will also occur around this time, preferably before the kickoff meeting, but as soon as possible. The scope of documentation may include executed batch record(s), test methods and qualification reports, specifications, bill of materials, development reports, etc.

Risk is further managed throughout the technology transfer process with regular project meetings to facilitate communication. This will include weekly teleconferences and face-to-face meetings at critical junctures. Information can also be shared through new and evolving technologies that can provide real time operational data as the process moves into manufacturing. Effective communication is critical throughout the process; regular interaction between SMEs is encouraged with the important caveat that project leaders and/or project managers are involved to ensure coordination and appropriate follow up.

Formal risk management tools will subsequently be used to support process characterization and process validation, but a quantitative risk assessment for a small company may have limited utility and the process relies more on involvement by more senior and experienced personnel.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念：生物製劑TT的風險管理現實

本節揭示了一個重要的實務真相：小型生技公司在TT啟動階段通常不做正式風險評估。風險管理的手段主要是：

  • 非正式層面：SME個人經驗 + due diligence audit（盡職調查審計）
  • 正式層面：在Change Control框架下執行，以及接近PPQ時進行FMEA

這並不代表這種做法最優，而是小公司資源有限的現實。CDMO應理解客戶可能沒有完整的風險文件，需要主動協助建立。

風險管理時序框架

TT階段        風險工具            目的
────────────────────────────────────────
CMO遴選期     Due Diligence Audit  非正式風險評估
              Site Visit          設施能力確認
              RFP/Proposal        技術可行性評估

合約後啟動    Change Control       正式變更管理
              Kick-off Meeting     風險溝通對齊
              Document Transfer    知識差距確認

工程批/
GMP批前       Collaborative FMEA   技術風險正式量化
              Critical Path Plan   時程風險管理

PPQ/PV期      Formal Risk Assess.  法規要求的書面風險評估
              Process Validation   生產一致性確認

重點提示：「量化風險評估對小公司效用有限」

文中直白地說：「a quantitative risk assessment for a small company may have limited utility」。這句話值得深思——傳統的ICH Q9 RPN評分（嚴重性 × 發生率 × 可偵測性）在數據不足的情況下，評分本身可能缺乏可信度。

在這種情況下，「有經驗的資深人員的判斷」往往比填滿一份RPN表格更有價值。監管機構對此也有共識：對新分子、新製程，質化風險評估加上專家判斷是被接受的方法。

關鍵是：無論用哪種方式，都要有文件記錄——哪怕只是「依據SME判斷，此項目風險可接受，理由如下」也比沒有記錄好。

比喻說明：Critical Path = 登山的關鍵路線

「Critical path activities」就是整個TT專案中，如果任何一個延誤，整個專案就無法按時完成的活動鏈。

就像登山隊要在日落前攻頂，必須識別哪條路線上有哪些必須在幾點前通過的節點。如果第一個節點就延誤了，後面再快也無法補回來。

在生物製劑TT中，典型的critical path包含：細胞株特性確認 → 長前置期物料到位 → 方法轉移完成 → 工程批執行 → 數據審查 → GMP批。任何一個環節阻塞，第一批GMP批的日期就會直接後移。

CDMO實務應用：Weekly Teleconference最佳實務

文中提到「weekly teleconferences」作為持續風險管理的機制。有效的每週例行會議結構：

  • Action Item Review（5分鐘）：確認上週行動項目完成狀態
  • Critical Path Status（10分鐘）：關鍵路徑活動是否如期進行
  • Issues & Risks（10分鐘）：新出現的問題，責任人和預計解決日期
  • Next Week Plan（5分鐘）：下週重要里程碑預告

關鍵原則：PM必須在場（確保follow-up），技術SME之間的討論不應繞過PM直接做決策，所有決策需有會議紀錄存檔以支持未來的查核與調查。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 文中提到due diligence audit是風險非正式評估的手段之一。若你是客戶的QA代表，due diligence audit的前三大重點檢查項目是什麼？
  2. 「Formal risk assessments are performed as part of change control」——在TT過程中，哪些事件最常觸發正式的變更管理流程？請舉三個例子。
  3. 若客戶堅持要CDMO在合約簽署前就完成完整的FMEA，你認為這個要求合理嗎？為什麼？
Section 9.5 — 技術轉移案例研究概述 (Technology Transfer Case Studies — Overview)

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer

9.5   Technology Transfer Case Studies

The first two case studies present specific technical, operational, and project management challenges that were faced from a client perspective during the technology transfer of two products, how these challenges were resolved, and what the outcome was for each.

The following three case studies are presented from the CMO perspective to illustrate technical challenges arising during technology transfer from small and mid-sized companies.

"The molecules in these case studies are primarily monoclonal antibodies (mAbs) but the lessons learned are generally applicable across all molecular classes."

Key themes covered across the five case studies:

  • Selection of the right CMO and managing the partnership
  • Dealing with limited development history or process knowledge
  • Managing technical challenges through collaborative problem-solving
  • Ensuring product comparability across the transfer
  • Effective program management and communication

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念：雙視角的學習設計

ISPE本附錄刻意安排了客戶視角（案例1–2）與CDMO視角（案例3–5）的雙面設計。這並非偶然，而是要讓讀者理解同一個技術轉移事件，在雙方眼中的感受和優先順序可能完全不同：

  • 客戶視角：關注的是時程、成本控制、產品可比性、法規路徑
  • CDMO視角：關注的是製程可行性、設備配置、文件完整性、責任邊界

理解對方的視角是成功TT夥伴關係的基礎。

重點提示：本節涵蓋範圍說明

本教學文件（section-06a）涵蓋至Section 9.5的概述性文字（p103結束）。五個個別案例研究的完整內容（9.5.1–9.5.5）收錄於下一個文件（section-06b）。

在閱讀具體案例前，建議先鞏固本節的核心框架：查核表差距分析（App.1）、三階段執行模型（9.3）、風險管理時序（9.4）。這些是理解案例的概念基礎。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 你認為「客戶視角」與「CDMO視角」在TT過程中最容易產生分歧的時間點是什麼？如何在合約設計上預防這種分歧？
  2. 文中強調mAb案例的「lessons learned可適用於所有分子類別」——你認為哪些mAb TT的教訓最不適合直接套用到細胞基因治療（CGT）的TT？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • 附錄一查核表是技術轉移啟動時的差距分析工具——為每項標記 Available / Partial / Missing，直接推動Risk Register建立；「Missing」項目即高風險項目
  • 大小分子差異：生物製劑需額外提供Cell Bank文件、Control Strategy、Waste/Vent特性；小分子需提供粒徑/多形體/溶解度/毒理/生體可用率等物理化學數據
  • 三階段實務模型：CMO Selection → Project Initiation → Project Execution，為ISPE六階段框架的小公司適用壓縮版
  • CMO遴選關鍵：RFP需足夠詳細（含製程細節/規格/BOM），至少進行1–2輪提案精煉，並對前兩名候選人進行due diligence audit
  • 風險管理現實：小型生技公司通常以非正式方式（SME經驗+稽核）管理早期風險，FMEA在接近PPQ時才正式引入；定期週例會是持續風險管理的基本機制
  • CDMO簽約前必備文件：Cell Bank Origin、Process Description + CPPs、Current Specifications + CQAs、至少3批歷史批次數據、初步穩定性數據
ISPE Good Practice Guide: Technology Transfer (3rd Edition) | p104–p112

本章學習目標

  • 理解五個真實生物製劑技術轉移案例的核心挑戰、應對策略與教訓
  • 掌握單株抗體（mAb）、融合蛋白（fusion protein）從早期臨床到商業規模轉移的風險模式
  • 學習緩衝液配製細節、細胞株可用性、設施適配等常見失效點，並建立預防性思維
  • 能夠根據這五個案例，為接收首個 mAb 的 CDMO 撰寫風險登記冊（risk register）的優先事項
  • 了解生物製劑 TT 的共同結論：哪些做法「有效」，哪些陷阱反覆出現
9.5.1 Biologics Case Study #1 — Transfer of a Phase 2 mAb Drug Substance

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer | p104–106

The first two case studies are interrelated in that they involve two products, one CMO company, and three CMO sites. The first case study describes a product in early phase 2 development that held significant clinical potential to move to a pivotal study. With the advent of breakthrough therapy designation and accelerated product development, the timelines for process optimization and the timeframe for gaining manufacturing experience to achieve a robust and reproducible manufacturing process is significantly reduced. Therefore, the process was transferred from the client's internal early phase manufacturing site to a US-based commercial CMO (site A) fairly early in clinical development.

This CMO was selected for the following reasons:

  • Commercial experience
  • Appropriate scale – 2000 L single-use bioreactors (SUB)
  • Available capacity – manufacturing slots available with ~12 months lead time
  • Good compliance history – FDA inspected as well as multiple other regulatory agency inspections
  • Technical skill/capability
  • Cost competitive

The client's internal manufacturing train was 250 L and 1,000 L, so transfer and scale-up to a 2,000 L scale was deemed low risk. However, manufacturing at the client site was performed with a low productivity cell line. Development of a new higher productivity cell line and establishment of a new Master Cell Bank (MCB) was nearing completion at the start of the technology transfer. Limited development work was performed at the client site and technology transfer was initiated prior to having completed full process development. Utilization of a Research Cell Bank (RCB) for initiation of technology transfer was also required since the MCB was not available yet.

Changes were made to the downstream process to enable facility fit and to improve process efficiency. A focused development and optimization approach leveraging CMO expertise and experience was taken for the downstream process to enable timely transfer of the process to GMP manufacturing. Changes in the downstream process included addition of a pH treatment step, change in depth filters, change in sequence of operations (Sartoclear® P filtration step moved from post to pre-SP-Sepharose® column chromatography), change in viral filter, and removal of a dilution step prior to loading the SP-Sepharose® column. An engineering run was performed to shake down the process and ensure process changes were effective and successfully scaled up to the manufacturing scale (2,000 L).

Table 9.2: Operational Challenges and Resolutions

Challenge Resolution
New, higher producing cell line not immediately available; no prior in-house manufacturing experience with new cell line Started development work with RCB, then switched to MCB for confirmation runs; agreed on enhanced RCB testing to allow shipment to CMO
Limited process optimization performed prior to technology transfer Performed focused process optimization work at CMO in parallel, utilizing the Ambr® system for upstream process; downstream process optimization included filter sizing studies, column load/cycling studies, etc.
Analytical changes: addition of Polysorbate 80 test method; transition from SDS-PAGE to capillary gel electrophoresis (CGE); incorporation of in-process buffer matrices into method qualification Leveraged platform assays when possible and utilized bridging studies to incorporate method changes
Viral clearance study issues – gaps in EU compliance at CMO and testing laboratory Limited certification of EU compliance (testing but not manufacturing EU certification) was available for regulatory submission. Follow-up Qualified Person certification required to ensure EU compliance
Manufacturing process changes requested by client; client needed a specific filter with low filter load to reduce host cell proteins Incorporated facility fit and manufacturing process changes into process optimization studies
Change in culture bags/filter trains; CMO had different culture bags; timeline for introducing client culture bag was lengthy Technical teams performed studies to support the change to the CMO's preferred culture bag/filter train
Managing deviations during manufacture and testing Fully engaged client and CMO QA organizations worked to resolve deviations/CAPAs in a timely manner
Client's lack of understanding of CMO's batch disposition/review process CMO flexibility permitted on-time disposition by real-time reviews/resolution and frequent meetings; accelerated release documentation transfer to drug product CMO permitted a smooth transition

Table 9.3: Project Management Challenges and Resolutions

Challenge Resolution
Managing unexpected events and timeline changes: new suite being built mid-transfer; suite construction, certification, and equipment qualification caused delay; additional process development/optimization work required Regular meetings of core team and SME sub-teams to ensure timelines were adjusted and technical issues were addressed; readjustment of scope to prioritize and manage costs/timeline
Lack of a joint steering committee to address issues early in technology transfer Engagement with senior site management to address issues; establishment of a formal joint steering committee structure to facilitate issue resolution
Result: Successful transfer and scale-up to 2,000 L. Timeline: ~15 months from project initiation to release of bulk drug substance. Slight delay, but acceleration of drug product release testing permitted meeting regulatory filing goals.

What Worked:

  • Technical competence and experience of CMO's process development/analytical development groups with technology transfer and scale-up
  • Defining changes required up front and implementing changes during initial development to monitor product quality
  • Coordination of analytical development/QC activities to complement product development activities
  • Dedicated project management and regular face-to-face and web-based meetings/updates – core team and sub-team meetings
  • Effective project management processes; document tracker with deliverables and utilization of online collaboration website for document sharing
  • Spirit of partnership and flexibility; commitment to improve and resolve issues
  • Studies co-completed during transfer to generate required data to sufficiently reduce manufacturing risk

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Breakthrough Therapy Designation（突破性療法指定）：FDA 給予臨床意義重大藥品的加速審核通道。後果是：開發時程壓縮，製程還沒完全確認就得啟動技術轉移。這對 CMO 而言是常態挑戰。

Research Cell Bank (RCB) vs. Master Cell Bank (MCB)：RCB 是研究用細胞庫，尚未完全符合 GMP 要求；MCB 是正式 GMP 細胞庫。TT 理論上應以 MCB 啟動，但 MCB 未就緒時只能先用 RCB，並需加強測試確認等效性。

Facility Fit（設施適配）：讓送出方的製程適應接收方的設備配置，包括設備尺寸、操作順序、現有耗材類型。不是「複製」製程，而是「移植」製程。

比喻說明 Analogy

這像是一位主廚（client）還在研發菜單（製程開發未完成），就把食譜送到新餐廳（CMO）去練習。新廚師不但要學食譜，還要同步改良食譜讓它適合新廚房的爐灶尺寸（facility fit）。這種「邊飛邊換引擎」的模式風險極高，需要雙方都有極強的技術能力和溝通機制。

重點提示 Key Notes

問題一：製程發展未完成就轉移。這是最高頻的生物製劑 TT 失敗起點。本案的解法是在 CMO 端同步進行製程優化——前提是 CMO 必須有足夠的製程開發能力。選 CMO 時「process development capability」不是加分項，是必要條件。

問題二：EU 病毒清除合規缺口。CMO 有 FDA 認證但缺 EU QP 認證，直接影響歐洲市場的藥品申請。多市場申請時，合規資格必須在 CMO 選擇階段就確認，事後補救代價極高。

問題三：批次放行流程不熟悉。客戶不了解 CMO 的批次審查機制，導致延遲。解法是靠 CMO 的靈活性，而非流程設計。這是一個「人治」解法，長期有風險。

CDMO 實務應用 Practical Application

若你的 CDMO 接到一個「breakthrough therapy」mAb 案件，製程開發尚未完成：

  • 立刻確認：MCB 預計完成日期，若延誤，RCB 的補充測試項目有哪些？
  • 設置「製程鎖定（process lock）」里程碑——在哪個節點之後不再接受送出方的改動請求？
  • 確認 CMO 端是否有 Ambr® 或類似高通量篩選系統，能夠承接優化工作？
  • 確認 EU QP 合規狀況——若客戶有歐洲市場計畫，此項必須在合約前確認。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼用 RCB 而非 MCB 開始 TT 工作是一種風險？需要哪些額外測試來降低此風險？
  2. 本案的 15 個月時程達成了嗎？有延誤嗎？延誤的根本原因是什麼？
  3. 缺乏 Joint Steering Committee 在早期造成了什麼問題？你的 CDMO 是否有類似的治理結構？
9.5.2 Biologics Case Study #2 — Late Clinical Phase mAb Transfer from One CMO to Another

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer | p107–109

The second case study involves the mAb intermediate component of an antibody-drug conjugate (ADC) in late stage clinical development. Technology transfer was driven by the need to move the mAb manufacture from the originally intended commercial CMO because of that company's decision to decommission the bioreactors that were planned for commercial manufacture of the product. In addition, there was no viable alternative available at the original CMO, so identification and selection of a new CMO was required.

Based on the prior experience with the CMO (site A) described in Biologics Case Study #1, another site in that CMO's network (site B) was selected for the following reasons:

  • Although site A was originally approached based on prior positive experience, capacity constraints indicated they could not meet the required ~12 month timeline. The client was directed to site B, a new facility in the CMO's network that had capacity and could accommodate the timeline.
  • Although the distance to site B (outside the US) was considered a potential challenge, the proximity of a CMO development site in the US (site C) was deemed a compensating attribute. Supporting optimization and small scale studies would be performed at site C.
  • CMO site B's host country offered financial incentive to perform pharmaceutical R&D activities in country.
  • Having multiple products with a single CMO was anticipated to provide efficiencies from a contractual, quality, and overall management perspective. However, there is also an associated risk with depending on a single CMO; this risk was mitigated by the fact that the CMO had a global footprint with multiple manufacturing sites in different countries.

At the time of initiating the technology transfer activities, the client was still in the process of establishing a new cell line suitable to meet regulatory expectations for commercialization. Utilization of a RCB for initiation of technology transfer was required because the MCB was unavailable due to delays in testing and challenges from differences in requirements for the receipt of new cell lines at the various CMO sites. Implementation of a modified filtration step following low pH viral inactivation was also required. However, due to time constraints, optimization prior to manufacturing was not possible. Based on the CMO's experience with the filter, it was considered low risk, and it was agreed that optimization could occur at a later date. Finally, a new bulk drug substance container was introduced to accommodate a change in storage temperature from 2–8°C to ≤ -65°C.

Table 9.4: Technical Challenges and Resolutions

ChallengeResolution
Cell line issues: new cell line still in development; manufacturing and testing delays at third-party cell bank manufacturer; inconsistent requirements between CMO sites for receipt of new cell banks Established criteria for receipt of RCB for development vs. MCB for GMP purposes; allowed flexibility to begin small scale work with RCB and transition to MCB once available
Implementation of alternate filtration step identified prior to transfer Agreed that optimization would be performed at a later date due to CMO's technical experience with the new filter
Change in bulk drug substance container and storage temperature Risk assessment determined risk to be low based on vendor white paper demonstrating compatibility with aqueous based solutions and performance of a short-term stability study to demonstrate compatibility with the new container closure system

Table 9.5: Operational Challenges and Resolutions

ChallengeResolution
Facility fit: scale and process changes required; equipment constraints (harvest vessels, single-use chromatography skid, no centrifuge, etc.) Performed small scale modeling exercise followed by focused small scale upstream and downstream confirmation run at CMO site C
Optimization of the cell expansion process Reduced the number of media required from four to one; evaluated process change at site C and transferred optimized process for manufacturing to site B
Media feed component transportation hazard classifications — a simple media feed component with no restrictions for US transport was now considered hazardous goods with strict requirements and restrictions on international shipping Evaluated raw material supply chain for potential regional sourcing options and adjusted raw material lead times based upon transportation, safety, and importation requirements

Table 9.6: Project Management Challenges and Resolutions

ChallengeResolution
Ensuring effective project team organization and structure between CMO sites A, B, and C Established sub-teams in addition to the core project team
Ensuring effective communication between three CMO sites and multiple client sites Regular meetings (online and face-to-face) for both core and sub-teams with documented minutes and action items; additional regular project management meetings to prepare and respond to open items
Integration of legacy procedures from prior CMO mergers into unified CMO procedures across three sites is a work in progress Integration and harmonization are corporate priority for CMO
Result: Timeline goal achieved — ~12 months from project initiation to bulk drug substance fill. Individual site requirements necessitated additional time to complete site-specific paperwork; however, all CMO sites agreed to expedited document reviews which allowed all processing to remain on schedule.
"While attractive in principle, it is important to understand that many of these [full-service CMO] networks have been established through merger and acquisition. While the business side of the merger and acquisition activities may progress quickly, it often takes time to fully integrate sites across different geographies, cultures, and corporate experience."

What Worked:

  • Technical competence and experience in technology transfer with well-defined process documentation
  • Small scale modeling and feasibility studies confirmed process operations; full scale engineering run confirmed small scale process and provided manufacturing with operational experience
  • Productive and appropriately scheduled meetings, including face-to-face kickoff, regular sub-team, and regular project management preparation and follow-up meetings
  • Person-in-place on-site at CMO site B helped develop relationship and allowed sponsor to gain first-hand experience in how the facility operates; also clearly aided in the transfer of information, clarification, and understanding of all unit operations
  • Client QA involvement early in the process provided opportunity to gain process knowledge prior to moving into GMP manufacturing

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Antibody-Drug Conjugate (ADC，抗體藥物複合物)：由 mAb 與細胞毒性小分子藥物透過連接子（linker）結合而成。製造上分兩段：mAb 生產（本案）+ 偶聯（conjugation）。因此 mAb 的轉移成功直接影響整個 ADC 計畫。

Person-in-Place（現場駐點人員）：客戶派駐在 CMO 現場的技術代表，可即時溝通、解決問題。本案明確指出其價值巨大。在跨國轉移中，這幾乎是必要的，尤其在首批 GMP 生產前。

CMO 整合後的「文化差異」風險：多個 CMO 透過併購形成網路，各站點的 SOP、文化、質量體系尚未統一，是一個真實但常被低估的風險。

比喻說明 Analogy

「單一 CMO 網路」的承諾，就像連鎖餐廳承諾「每家分店都一樣」。但若這個連鎖品牌是最近收購了十家不同風格的獨立餐廳，廚師的訓練、食材供應商、甚至點餐系統都不同，吃起來的體驗就會有天壤之別。客戶需要主動了解每個「分店」的實際狀況，而不是只看品牌名稱。

重點提示 Key Notes

國際原料運輸的隱形風險：一個在美國國內完全無限制運輸的培養基成分，跨國運輸時可能被歸類為「危險品」，需要特殊包裝、文件、甚至航空禁運。這類供應鏈風險必須在 CMO 選定後立即進行全面評估，不能等到製造時才發現。

容器儲存溫度變更（2–8°C → ≤-65°C）：看似是小改動，實際上牽涉容器相容性、穩定性數據、運輸驗證，以及下游 ADC 偶聯製程的接收條件。每一個步驟都必須有數據支持。本案以廠商白皮書加短期穩定性研究作為依據，是務實但需記錄充分風險評估的做法。

多站點 CMO 網路風險評估框架

多 CMO 站點風險 =
  (各站點的技術熟悉度差異)
+ (SOP/QMS 整合完成度)
+ (跨國法規與供應鏈複雜度)
+ (溝通時區與語言障礙)

緩解措施：
  Person-in-place + 明確的跨站點溝通結構
  + 獨立的技術子團隊（upstream / downstream / analytical）

CDMO 實務應用 Practical Application

若你是接收方 CMO（site B），首次與客戶合作且需在 12 個月內完成首批 GMP 批次：

  • 第一步：確認所有原料的進口許可與運輸分類（尤其是有機溶劑或特殊培養基成分）
  • 第二步：評估自身設備與客戶製程的落差（無離心機？使用單次性層析系統？），先做小規模模擬確認可行性
  • 第三步：建議客戶派遣 Person-in-Place，至少在 GMP 前的 Engineering Run 期間全程駐守
  • 第四步：確認客戶的 QA 在首批 GMP 生產前就深度參與，避免批次放行時才發現質量體系認知差距

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 本案選擇 CMO site B（而非 site A）的主要原因是什麼？其中哪個原因事後來看是最關鍵的？
  2. 「單一 CMO 網路」的商業優勢與風險各是什麼？如何在合約中設計 mitigation？
  3. 媒體成分被列為「危險品」這個問題，在 TT 流程的哪個階段應該被識別出來？
9.5.3 Biologics Case Study #3 — Buffer Formulation Discrepancy in Protein A Purification

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer | p109–110

An mAb purification process was developed at a small biotechnology company and transferred to a CMO for evaluation at laboratory scale, prior to scale-up to a non-GMP pilot and first GMP clinical batch. The process consisted of a Protein A chromatography step, low pH virus inactivation, and pH adjustment followed by cation exchange and anion exchange chromatography steps.

At the sending unit, the product was eluted from Protein A with acetate buffer pH 3.2 and the product eluted from the column within the required range for the viral inactivation step. The eluate was pH adjusted to pH 5.0 for the cation exchange step using 1 part product to 4 parts titrant. Prior to manufacture of the first GMP batch, a laboratory scale and pilot scale evaluation was performed at the receiving unit. During the laboratory scale evaluation at the receiving unit, two issues arose with the Protein A step.

A root cause analysis (Ishikawa diagram) was performed on the Protein A step. A number of items were highlighted for further investigation between the two units, relating to elution buffer and titrant preparation. During the transfer, only the names of the buffers were shared and not the preparation details. Two key differences were identified:

  • At the sending unit, the elution buffer and the titrant were prepared using the trihydrate salt, compared to use of the anhydrous salt at the receiving unit.
  • At the sending unit, the elution buffer was titrated with hydrochloric acid, compared to titration with acetic acid at the receiving unit, which resulted in much higher buffering capacity.

Table 9.7: Challenges and Resolutions

ChallengeResolution
The pH of the Protein A eluate, although in the viral inactivation range, was much lower than expected The two issues were linked. Elution buffer was reformulated using trihydrate salt and acetic acid to achieve the required acetate concentration. The new formulations and the original formulations were compared side by side on two Protein A cycles. With the new formulations, the pH of the eluted product was now above the required viral inactivation range. Further evaluation resulted in adjustments to the acetate concentration in the elution buffer and titrant.
Approximately double the volume of titrant was required to adjust the pH of the Protein A eluate to pH 5.0 Preparation of the titrant with the trihydrate salt and adjustment of the acetate concentration resulted in the expected volume of titrant being added for pH adjustment to pH 5.0.
Result: Formulation of the elution buffer with the trihydrate salt and adjustment of the acetate concentration resulted in the eluted product pH achieving the required pH range for viral inactivation. Preparation of the titrant with the trihydrate salt and adjustment of the acetate concentration resulted in the expected volume of titrant being added for pH adjustment to pH 5.0.

What Worked:

  • Good communication between technical SMEs at sending and receiving units: the unexpected performance of the Protein A step and potential causes were flagged for the receiving unit, so details of buffer and titrant preparation could be compared quickly and adjusted as the laboratory scale evaluation was ongoing
  • Formulation of the elution buffer facilitated preparation at scale in the GMP facility

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Trihydrate vs. Anhydrous Salt（三水合物 vs. 無水鹽）：同一種化學物質的兩種形態。三水合物含有結晶水，相同「克數」的三水合物含有較少的實際活性成分。若配方以「mg/mL」為準，用錯形態會導致緩衝能力（buffering capacity）不同，pH 行為因此出現偏差。

低 pH 病毒滅活（Low pH Viral Inactivation）：生物製劑的重要病毒清除步驟。Protein A 洗脫的 eluate 通常 pH 在 3–4 之間，需維持一定時間以確保病毒被滅活。若 pH 偏低，可能增加蛋白質變性風險；若偏高，病毒滅活效果可能不足。pH 控制精確性是這一步的核心。

Ishikawa Diagram（石川圖，魚骨圖）：結構化根本原因分析工具，系統性列出可能導致問題的各類原因（人、機、料、法、環境）。是 GMP 偏差調查的標準工具之一。

比喻說明 Analogy

這個案例就像兩個廚師都說「加一茶匙鹽」，但一個用的是粗鹽（trihydrate，顆粒大，一茶匙的重量少），另一個用的是細鹽（anhydrous，顆粒密，一茶匙的重量多）。食譜上只寫「一茶匙鹽」，沒有說明是哪種鹽，結果味道完全不同。這就是「只傳遞緩衝液名稱，不傳遞配製細節」的危險。

重點提示 Key Notes

這是最常見、也最容易預防的 TT 失敗模式之一：緩衝液配製細節未納入轉移文件。正確的 TT 文件應包含：鹽的化學形態（trihydrate / anhydrous）、滴定酸的種類、pH 調整操作順序、水質要求（WFI vs. purified water）。僅傳遞「緩衝液名稱」是不完整的技術轉移。

低 pH 滅活的 pH 範圍必須有安全邊際：本案 pH 比預期更低，雖仍在病毒滅活範圍內，但已接近可能造成產品損傷的區域。這種「剛好在範圍內」的情況，在驗證時必須確認操作空間（design space）足夠寬裕。

緩衝液轉移的完整文件清單

最低要求（必傳）：
  1. 緩衝液名稱及目標 pH / 濃度
  2. 鹽類的化學形態（trihydrate vs. anhydrous）
  3. 滴定所用酸/鹼的種類與濃度
  4. 配製順序（先加哪種成分）
  5. 水質規格（注射用水 WFI / 純化水）
  6. 過濾規格（0.2 μm，使用前 / 使用後）
  7. 貯存溫度與有效期限

推薦附加（降低誤解風險）：
  - 配製實例（以具體批量計算）
  - 已執行配製批次的 pH 實測範圍
  - 代表性緩衝曲線（titration curve）

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 若你是接收方 QC，在接到送出方的緩衝液配方後，應該主動確認哪些資訊？
  2. 為什麼用鹽酸（HCl）滴定和用醋酸（acetic acid）滴定的緩衝能力不同？這對 Protein A 洗脫步驟有什麼影響？
  3. 這個問題在實驗室規模就被發現，如果直接進行 GMP 生產才發現，後果會是什麼？
9.5.4 Biologics Case Study #4 — Transfer of a Challenging IgM Molecule

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer | p110–112

This case study relates to transferring a process from a small biotechnology company with process development capabilities to a CMO with process development, scale-up, and GMP capabilities. A good relationship had been established between the two parties from collaborations on previous process transfers, process development, and GMP batch manufacture.

In this case study, the product was a very large, challenging antibody molecule (immunoglobulin M, IgM) which could not be purified using resins already available at the CMO. The plan was to evaluate the process at laboratory scale and scale-up to non-GMP pilot scale before manufacturing a GMP batch.

As there were no batch records or development reports available from the sending unit, the process was transferred using a transfer document developed at the CMO. In addition to process details, this transfer document included a request for information from the sending unit on product stability at high or low pH, any tendency to aggregate, evidence of instability in particular buffers, solubility issues at high or low conductivity, and highest concentration that the product has been demonstrated to be stable. In addition, SOPs at the CMO were outlined in this transfer document, including flow rate ranges (based on equipment available), resin cleaning conditions, and generic hold times. This helped to align procedures at both sites.

The process transferred to the CMO included a Protein A step, anion exchange (AEX) chromatography, and ultraviolet (UV) treatment. Final formulation development was ongoing during the transfer. Initially, the process was evaluated at 10 L bioreactor scale at the CMO, then scaled up and evaluated in two non-GMP pilot batches. SMEs from the sending unit were present during key processing steps at the receiving unit to be able to discuss, advise, and help resolve technical issues real time.

Table 9.8: Challenges and Resolutions

ChallengeResolution
New Protein A resin for CMO which required a new (vibrational) packing method CMO evaluated the vibrational method with on-site input from the vendor
Much lower than expected recovery on Protein A column during laboratory scale evaluation at CMO Reduced loading capacity and flow rates at CMO. Sending unit performed further evaluation to align with CMO data. Further evaluation on scale-up at CMO to define final loading capacity.
Higher than expected conductivity on elution from the Protein A column, which would impact performance of AEX step Introduced ultrafiltration step at CMO to reduce conductivity. Subsequently, an alternative Protein A elution buffer was evaluated at sending unit, which eliminated the requirement for an ultrafiltration step.
New AEX column type for CMO, no flow rates transferred from sending unit CMO used manufacturer's recommendations, with on-site support from vendor on scale-up
AEX column gave inconsistent process performance results on scale-up and poor impurity removal at CMO Sending unit developed alternate AEX step (traditional resin), which increased throughput and improved impurity removal
Molecule was too large for 20 nm nanofiltration; sending unit recommended UV treatment, but no experimental work had been performed prior to transfer to CMO CMO hired UV equipment; this required evaluation at non-GMP pilot scale due to material quantities required. Developed step, but resulted in increased % aggregates.
On scale-up at CMO, product concentration post-AEX step was too low for UV treatment Introduced a concentration step prior to UV treatment, using CMO platform conditions
Unknown impact of UV treatment on virus reduction GMP virus reduction study was performed by the CMO to define operating conditions
No third step was initially developed for aggregate removal at the sending unit CMO and sending unit evaluated two options in parallel; third chromatography step further established at sending unit and evaluated on scale-up at CMO
Limited analytical data at sending unit as impurity methods had not been established Use of CMO platform methods for impurities
Limited analytical data at CMO as product quality methods had not been transferred from sending unit Samples sent from CMO to sending unit for product quality analysis
Result: The purification process was evaluated over a 12-month timeframe, at laboratory and non-GMP pilot scale. The final batch was manufactured with the revised, three chromatography step process. However, although product quality and impurity levels in drug substance were acceptable, the cumulative recovery was <10%. Consequently, cost of goods was excessive. At this point, the program was placed on hold by the client, due to other more promising molecules in their pipeline and the process was never transferred to GMP manufacturing.

What Worked:

  • Throughout the technology transfer process, both the sending and receiving units gained a huge amount of experience and maintained a good working relationship
  • Technical competence at both units — data compiled real time for sharing and discussing; SMEs worked together to resolve issues real time
  • New technologies were implemented which required support from vendors

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

IgM（免疫球蛋白 M）：分子量約為 IgG（mAb）的 5–10 倍，無法用標準 Protein A 親和力層析（因 Protein A 主要針對 IgG Fc 區域）純化。製程開發難度遠高於一般 mAb，每個步驟都充滿未知數。

Cumulative Recovery（累積回收率）：多個純化步驟的回收率連乘積。若每步 70%，三步後：70% × 70% × 70% = 34%。本案 <10% 意味著某些步驟回收率極低，導致成本效益無法成立。

UV Treatment for Virus Reduction（UV 病毒清除）：當分子太大無法通過 20 nm 奈米過濾膜（nanofiltration）時的替代病毒清除方案。但 UV 對大分子蛋白質可能促進聚集體（aggregates）形成，需要精確控制劑量和操作條件。

比喻說明 Analogy

IgM 的製程轉移就像嘗試用做西餐的廚房設備（標準 CMO 層析管柱）來做傳統糕點（IgM）。工具本來就不合用，每一步都要臨時找新方法、借新設備、改流程。做出來的糕點雖然「可以吃」（品質合格），但損耗太大（回收率 <10%），一塊糕點的成本是正常的 10 倍。老闆（客戶）最後決定換一道菜（其他管線分子）。這是一個無論技術上多努力，商業上仍然失敗的案例。

重點提示 Key Notes

沒有批次記錄就啟動轉移：這是本案最大的根本問題。送出方沒有批次記錄和開發報告，接收方必須自行開發轉移文件框架，要求送出方填寫關鍵產品知識（pH 穩定性、聚集傾向、溶解度等）。這個做法雖然彌補了部分缺口，但轉移過來的製程基本上是一個「待完成」的製程。

UV 病毒清除步驟在轉移前未驗證：送出方只是「建議」使用 UV，沒有任何實驗數據。這意味著接收方要在 CMO 端從零開發一個全新的病毒清除步驟，並且需要在非 GMP 規模進行評估（因為需要大量物料）。這是一個典型的「不完整製程轉移」。

<10% 回收率的商業意義：以 mAb 商業規模計算，若正常製程回收率為 60%，改善空間在 50 倍以上。低回收率直接推高 Cost of Goods (COGS)，在競爭性產品定價環境中幾乎無法立足。技術可行性 ≠ 商業可行性。

CDMO 實務應用 Practical Application

接到一個「沒有批次記錄」的非標準分子（如 IgM、双特異性抗體）詢價時：

  • 立即要求送出方填寫「分子特性問卷」：pH / 濃度穩定性、聚集傾向、特殊溶解度需求、已知製程問題
  • 評估自身是否有相應的設備（特殊填料、UV 設備、UF/DF 能力）
  • 在合約中明確區分：「技術轉移」vs.「製程開發代工」——後者風險更高、費用應更高
  • 設定「go/no-go」里程碑，以回收率、雜質去除率等指標為觸發點，避免無止境投入資源

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 本案的最終結果是「品質合格但回收率 <10%」，程序被叫停。這算是技術轉移「失敗」嗎？為什麼？
  2. 如果你是 CMO 的項目主管，在哪個里程碑點應該向客戶提出「此製程可能無商業可行性」的警示？
  3. 「CMO 開發轉移文件，要求送出方填寫分子知識」這種做法有什麼優缺點？
9.5.5 Biologics Case Study #5 — Fusion Protein Transfer from Early Clinical CMO to Scale-up CMO

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer | p112

For the final case study, the process was transferred from one CMO where the process had been developed and manufactured to a second CMO with the intent of scaling up the process, due to increased material requirements beyond the equipment capabilities of the first CMO.

A SharePoint site was set up between the biotech company and the second CMO as a way of exchanging confidential information, including process development reports, executed batch records, in-process testing, drug substance testing, and trend analysis of the GMP batches for upstream and downstream processes. During the laboratory scale evaluation at the receiving unit, an issue arose on the second chromatography step in the purification process.

Table 9.9: Challenges and Resolutions

ChallengeResolution
Tight timeframe – 10 L laboratory scale evaluation being initiated only one month after receipt of technology transfer information package; a non-GMP 400 L pilot scale batch was initiated 10 weeks later; the first GMP engineering batch in the larger CMO manufacturing facility was seven months later Experimental work was initiated under a "Letter of Intent" and the formal Amendment was signed approximately two months later detailing the stages of work; increased number of teleconferences; process data was shared in multiple documents, including batch records from the CMO and a summary development report generated by the biotechnology company; development laboratory at the second CMO prepared process descriptions based on the data available, which were reviewed by SMEs from the biotechnology company before proceeding with laboratory work
Product did not elute as expected from the second chromatography column; breakthrough was observed during a post-load wash, which significantly impacted the % recovery Investigation resulted in identification of an error in chromatography resin type used

An initial investigation was performed. Process step details were compared between the batch records from the sending unit, the process description generated at the receiving unit, and data recorded in the laboratory notebook. Initial root causes considered were related to buffer pH and conductivity specifications as the ranges transferred were broad. However, all buffers prepared at the second CMO were within the required ranges.

Investigation resulted in an error in chromatography resin type used. The correct resin had been specified, yet the wrong resin was dispensed. A documentation and verification gap allowed an incorrect resin to be used without detection.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Letter of Intent（意向書）先啟動工作：在正式合約簽署前，以意向書為依據開始實驗工作。這在時間緊迫的生物製劑 TT 中相當普遍，但需注意：若後續談判破裂，雙方的費用歸屬和知識產權歸屬可能產生爭議。合約談判應與技術工作並行，不能無限期拖延。

Wrong Resin Used（使用錯誤填料）：正確填料規格已記載在製程文件中，但實驗室領料時發出了錯誤的填料，且沒有被檢查出來。這是一個純粹的操作和文件管控失敗，而非技術問題。

比喻說明 Analogy

這就像醫院藥局開出了正確的藥名，但藥師從貨架上拿錯了藥瓶，因為沒有雙人確認機制，直接發給了護理師。病人吃錯藥不是因為醫生開錯處方，而是執行環節缺少了驗證步驟。在 GMP 生產中，任何物料的使用都需要「兩人確認 + 標籤驗證」作為防呆機制。

重點提示 Key Notes

「時程壓力」是最容易觸發程序跳步的因素：本案在收到技術轉移文件後 1 個月就開始實驗，10 週後就進行 pilot 批次。這種速度下，材料確認、程序審查容易被壓縮。「填料用錯了」這件事，在時間充裕的情況下很可能會在實驗前的 SOP 審查就被發現。

TT 文件的「傳遞 → 轉化 → 執行」三層驗證：本案的問題發生在「執行」層：正確規格已在文件中，但實際操作時沒有驗證領料是否符合規格。完整的 TT 體系需要確保每一層都有獨立的查核機制，包括：(1) 文件是否完整傳遞；(2) 接收方是否正確理解並轉化為本地 SOP；(3) 執行時是否按 SOP 操作並驗證物料。

CDMO 實務應用 Practical Application

針對「使用錯誤填料」這類執行層錯誤，CDMO 應建立：

  • 物料雙人確認制度：層析填料、培養基、緩衝液成分，在使用前需由第二人對照 SOP 驗證批號、規格、外觀。
  • 填料登記冊（resin log）：記錄每批填料的使用歷史、清洗次數、性能測試結果，確保正確追蹤。
  • 「超緊時程」紅旗機制：當 TT 計畫時程極度壓縮時，QA 應啟動強化監督模式——增加實驗前審查會議，確保速度不犧牲程序完整性。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 「使用錯誤填料」應該如何在 GMP 體系中被分類（計畫外事件、偏差、CAPA）？調查報告應包含哪些要素？
  2. Letter of Intent 先啟動工作的做法有哪些商業和法律風險？如何在合約中預先限制這些風險？
  3. 本案的 TT 時程（1 個月→實驗室，10 週→pilot，7 個月→GMP）與你認知的一般 mAb TT 時程相比，是快還是慢？合理嗎？
9.6 Conclusions: Lessons Learned from Biologics Technology Transfer

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE Tech Transfer | Appendix 2 Synthesis

The five biologics case studies presented in this appendix — spanning Phase 2 mAb transfers, CMO-to-CMO late-stage transfers, purification process evaluations, and complex molecule development — collectively illustrate the unique complexity of biologics technology transfer compared to small molecule manufacturing.

Across all five case studies, several universal themes emerge:

Theme 1: Cell line and cell bank availability is a recurrent critical path item. In Case Studies #1 and #2, the unavailability of the Master Cell Bank (MCB) at the start of transfer required use of a Research Cell Bank (RCB), adding risk and requiring enhanced testing. Cell line readiness — including third-party cell bank testing timelines — must be factored into every biologic TT project plan as a potential critical path constraint.

Theme 2: Process development completion is prerequisite to successful transfer. Multiple case studies describe transfers initiated before process development was complete. While sometimes unavoidable under breakthrough therapy or accelerated development timelines, this approach requires a CMO partner with strong in-house development capability and a clear, contractually defined boundary between "technology transfer" and "process development."

Theme 3: Documentation detail — not just document titles — must be transferred. Case Study #3 demonstrates that transferring buffer names without preparation details led to a reproducible but unexpected pH result. Complete transfer packages must include chemical forms of salts, titration reagent identities, preparation sequences, water quality specifications, and working concentration ranges.

Theme 4: Facility fit and equipment equivalence require proactive small-scale modeling. All case studies involve some degree of facility fit work — changes in scale, equipment type, or process sequence. The successful transfers used small-scale modeling at a development site (site C in Case Study #2) to confirm process feasibility before committing to full-scale GMP manufacturing.

Theme 5: Communication infrastructure is as important as technical capability. Across every case study, the "What Worked" section highlights dedicated project management, regular cross-functional meetings (core team + SME sub-teams), documented action items, and — particularly for international transfers — person-in-place representation. These are not "soft" factors; they are structural enablers of transfer success.

Theme 6: Commercial feasibility must be assessed alongside technical feasibility. Case Study #4 demonstrates that a technically successful process development effort (achieving acceptable product quality) can still result in program termination if cumulative recovery is insufficient to support commercial cost-of-goods. Go/no-go criteria based on yield and COGS should be defined at project initiation.

Theme 7: Regulatory compliance scope must be confirmed before CMO selection. Case Study #1 reveals a gap in EU viral clearance certification that was not identified until late in the transfer. For products targeting multiple markets, regulatory compliance coverage (FDA, EMA, PMDA, etc.) must be a CMO selection criterion, not an afterthought.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

五個案例的共同模式總結

讀完五個案例，可以歸納出生物製劑 TT 的「失敗七宗罪」——這些問題不是偶然，而是跨案例反覆出現的結構性缺陷：

  • MCB 未就緒就啟動：案例 #1、#2
  • 製程開發未完成就轉移：案例 #1、#2、#4
  • 緩衝液細節未傳遞：案例 #3
  • 設施適配未充分評估：案例 #2、#4
  • 分析方法未完整轉移：案例 #4
  • EU 法規合規未提前確認：案例 #1
  • 操作層執行驗證缺失（錯誤填料）：案例 #5

比喻說明 Analogy

生物製劑 TT 就像把一家米其林星餐廳的「靈魂」搬到新城市。轉移的不只是食譜，還有廚師的手感、食材的供應商、廚房設備的習慣，甚至顧客預期。每一個細節的缺失，都可能讓「同一道菜」在新地點失去靈魂。五個案例的教訓是：只傳遞「食譜名稱」是不夠的，必須傳遞整個「烹飪哲學」。

重點提示：CDMO 接收首個 mAb 的風險登記冊（Risk Register）Top 10

  1. [高] MCB 可用性延遲 → 影響首批 GMP 時程
  2. [高] 製程開發未完成 → 需在 CMO 端同步開發，成本/時程不可控
  3. [高] EU/多市場法規資格缺口 → 影響藥品上市申請完整性
  4. [中] 緩衝液配製細節缺失 → 導致製程重現性問題
  5. [中] 分析方法轉移不完整 → 無法進行完整的可比性評估
  6. [中] 設施適配差異（設備、規模）→ 需額外開發工作
  7. [中] 國際原料供應鏈中斷或危險品分類問題
  8. [中] 病毒清除合規差距（CMO 認證範圍 vs. 目標市場要求）
  9. [低-中] 客戶批次放行流程與 CMO 不一致導致延誤
  10. [低-中] 操作層物料管控失誤（錯誤填料、錯誤試劑）

生物製劑 TT 成功的必要條件矩陣

成功維度       | 案例 #1 | 案例 #2 | 案例 #3 | 案例 #4 | 案例 #5
────────────────────────────────────────────────────
製程完整性      |  部分   |  部分   |  完整   |  缺乏   |  完整
MCB 就緒       |  否     |  否     |  是     |  是     |  是
文件完整性      |  部分   |  良好   |  不足   |  缺乏   |  良好
設施適配評估    |  是     |  是     |  是     |  是     |  是
溝通機制       |  良好   |  良好   |  良好   |  良好   |  良好
商業可行性      |  是     |  是     |  是     |  否     |  是
最終結果       |  成功   |  成功   |  成功   |  中止   |  進行中

CDMO 實務應用 Practical Application

基於五個案例，為你的 CDMO 建立「mAb 技術轉移審查清單（Pre-Transfer Readiness Checklist）」：

  • MCB 是否可用？若否，RCB 的補充測試計畫是什麼？
  • 製程開發報告（PDR）是否涵蓋所有單元操作，包括緩衝液配製細節？
  • 分析方法是否完整轉移？可比性評估計畫是否確定？
  • 設施適配差距評估（Facility Fit Gap Assessment）是否完成？
  • 目標市場的法規合規資格（FDA / EMA / PMDA）是否確認？
  • 病毒清除策略和 CMO 的相應認證是否匹配？
  • 供應鏈評估（尤其是跨國原料運輸）是否完成？
  • 商業可行性的 go/no-go 里程碑是否在合約中明確？

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 五個案例中，哪一個你認為教訓最具普遍性，可以應用到任何複雜生物製劑的 TT 中？
  2. 如果你只能給一個「首次接 mAb」的 CDMO 一條建議，你會給什麼？
  3. 「技術成功但商業失敗」（案例 #4）對 CDMO 而言意味著什麼？如何在合約設計中保護 CDMO？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • 案例 #1（Phase 2 mAb）：製程未完成就轉移，MCB 未就緒用 RCB，EU 合規缺口——這三個問題是生物製劑 TT 的高頻風險，需要 CMO 具備強大的製程開發能力與靈活的 QA 體系。
  • 案例 #2（CMO-to-CMO ADC 中間體）：跨國多站點 CMO 網路的隱性風險——整合程度不足、國際原料供應鏈、地區法規差異，Person-in-Place 是跨國轉移的關鍵成功因素。
  • 案例 #3（緩衝液配製差異）：「只傳遞名稱、不傳遞細節」是導致 Protein A 步驟 pH 異常的根本原因。完整的緩衝液 TT 文件必須包含鹽的化學形態和滴定試劑種類。
  • 案例 #4（IgM 困難分子）：技術上可以成功，商業上不可行。<10% 的累積回收率導致 COGS 過高，程序被叫停。TT 計畫必須設定商業可行性的 go/no-go 里程碑。
  • 案例 #5（融合蛋白 CMO-to-CMO）：時程壓力下的操作層缺失——使用錯誤層析填料。速度不能犧牲物料管控程序；Letter of Intent 先啟動的模式需要配套完善的文件確認機制。
  • 共同結論：生物製劑 TT 的成功需要「技術能力 + 文件完整性 + 溝通基礎設施 + 商業判斷」四者兼備。任何一個維度的缺失，都可能導致整個計畫失敗。
7

Chapter 7: Appendix 3: Small Molecule Case Studies

附錄三：小分子案例研究 | p113-p122

ISPE Good Practice Guide: Technology Transfer (3rd Edition) | p113–p122

本章學習目標

  • 了解小分子 API 技術轉移的主要挑戰：供應鏈壓力、法規差異、跨國 QMS 解讀落差
  • 分析三個真實案例：供應鏈驅動轉移、分析方法轉移的 QMS 對齊、CDMO 開發至商業化轉移
  • 掌握五階段技術轉移流程模型與高階風險評估矩陣的應用方式
  • 理解 CPP 知識轉移中「文件記錄」與「實際操作」之間的落差如何影響轉移成敗
  • 從每個案例中提取普遍性的經驗教訓，並應用於 CDMO 的接收場地規劃
10.1 Summary — 章節摘要

原文內容 Original Text

ISPE

This chapter focuses on key challenges associated with global API technology transfers and provides examples of potential technical, cultural, and organizational gaps between the sending and receiving units. Addressing these challenges and gaps can enhance program management of technology transfers across markets.

The technology transfer of APIs follows similar steps as those presented in the case studies for biologics in Chapter 9 and as explained in detail in this Guide. In this chapter, three case studies for small molecule API technology transfers are presented:

  • The first two case studies show challenges related to non-technical differences between the sending and receiving units — both sites within the same large, global pharmaceutical company.
  • The third case study presents technical challenges of a Contract Development and Manufacturing Organization (CDMO) as they develop and manufacture an API for a large, global pharmaceutical company with a business plan to market the API as a virtual company.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Global API Technology Transfer (全球 API 技術轉移)：將 API 製造製程從一個地點遷移至另一個地點的正式過程，涵蓋製程知識、分析方法、法規文件的完整交接。小分子 API 轉移雖然化學上相對成熟，但跨國的組織與文化落差往往才是最大的挑戰。

三大案例類型：

  • 案例 1：供應鏈驅動（商業→商業）
  • 案例 2：方法轉移的 QMS 對齊（開發→商業）
  • 案例 3：CDMO 開發至商業化（技術開發→植物規模）

比喻說明 Analogy

三個案例就像同一道菜在不同廚房重現：第一個是把已上市的菜移到新廚房繼續賣；第二個是新菜移廠但還在測試階段；第三個是委外廚房從頭開發再放大到量產。每個情境的挑戰完全不同——但都需要菜譜（製程文件）、食材（原料）和廚師技能（操作知識）的完整交接。

重點提示 Key Notes

本章最重要的洞察：即使轉移發生在同一公司內部的兩個廠區，技術、文化、組織的落差仍然存在且影響深遠。這打破了「內部轉移比外部容易」的常見假設。對 CDMO 而言，這意味著接收客戶的製程時，不能假設對方的文件已經完整——必須主動識別知識缺口。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼同一公司內部的兩個廠區之間的技術轉移也會有「文化落差」？請舉例說明。
  2. 小分子 API 轉移與生物製劑轉移（第 9 章）在挑戰的性質上有何主要差異？
10.2 Main Challenges — 主要挑戰

原文內容 Original Text

Supply chains for the manufacture of APIs are constantly requiring technology transfers to be performed in the pursuit of lower cost options, process improvements, market requirements, and continuity of supply. In recent years, many of the API technology transfers have been from domestic to global manufacturing sites, often at an external company.

Development of API processes has also moved to centralized, global development centers that do not have large scale manufacturing capabilities; this requires a technology transfer to another site for commercial production.

The movement to global supply chains for API manufacture requires the technology transfer to understand the differences between the sending and receiving units, specifically:

  • Differences in their Quality Management Systems (QMSs)
  • Risk tolerance levels
  • Operating/compliance standards

These differences need to be identified early in the technology transfer process so they can be addressed and factored into the overall transfer plan.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

四大驅動技術轉移的業務因素：

  • 降低成本 (Lower Cost)：尋找生產成本更低的地點，常見為從西方國家遷往印度、中國等地
  • 製程改良 (Process Improvement)：在轉移過程中同步升級製程
  • 市場要求 (Market Requirements)：當地法規、進口限制或市場准入要求在當地生產
  • 供應連續性 (Continuity of Supply)：降低單一廠點的供應風險

風險識別框架 Risk Identification Framework

轉移成功的三大前提條件：
1. QMS 差異識別（法規解讀、文件要求）
   → 需在轉移「計畫期」完成，而非執行中才發現
2. 風險容忍度對齊
   → 送出方與接收方對「可接受偏差」的標準是否一致？
3. 操作/合規標準比對
   → 哪些 SOP 需要在接收廠重新建立？

重點提示 Key Notes

全球化供應鏈的趨勢使得跨國技術轉移成為常態，但隨之而來的是：API 開發中心往往不具備商業規模製造能力（純粹的研發中心）。這意味著「開發至商業」的知識轉移幾乎必然涉及跨組織、跨文化的落差。對 CDMO 而言，這正是商機所在——客戶需要有能力接收早期開發知識並放大至商業規模的夥伴。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 當技術轉移的主要驅動力是「降低成本」時，最容易被忽略的技術知識是哪些？
  2. 如何在轉移計畫初期識別兩個廠點之間的 QMS 差異？你會使用什麼工具？
10.3 Technology Transfer Process — 技術轉移流程

原文內容 Original Text

As shown in Chapter 1, ICH Q10 [1] defines the product lifecycle elements. Chapter 3 then defines the technology transfer activities as six distinct phases. In the first two case studies, a modified technology transfer process (five stage process as shown in Figure 10.1) was implemented to facilitate the cross-functional framework of the transfer as well as regular review of the transfer risks.

In the example process depicted in Figure 10.1, defined checkpoints with a steering committee are used to evaluate risk and provide approval prior to moving to the next stage. The typical functions required in each stage of this transfer model are also shown.

In this example technology transfer process, early feasibility is defined as the first stage, incorporating key technical functions, to help assess high level risk which is then used to develop the technology transfer charter. An example of a high level risk evaluation for a technology transfer is provided in Table 10.1.

Table 10.1: Example High Level Technology Transfer Risk Evaluation for Feasibility Stage
Sending Unit Receiving Unit New Product Same/Single Market New/Multiple Market(s) Existing Production Line New Production Line Equipment Change Process Change >10x Scale-up
Site 1Site 1LowLowLowN/AMedMed/HighMed/HighHigh
Site 1Site 1HighHighHighLow/MedMedHighN/AHigh
Site 1Site 2LowLowLowLowMedMed/HighMed/HighHigh
Site 1Site 2HighHighHighMedMedHighN/AHigh

The feasibility stage is often used for site selection, which is discussed in more detail in Chapter 9. Detailed risk assessment is then performed in the second stage using a broader cross-functional team to identify all elements of the knowledge transfer needed to perform a successful technology transfer.

The third case study is from a CDMO (based in India) that performs both API process development and API manufacturing. Figure 10.2 shows an example CDMO technology transfer model. This model incorporates detailed elements related to the process development and the information required from the ongoing process development for the knowledge transfer. The CDMO completes the development phase by performing laboratory scale reproducibility batches to mimic plant conditions and hold times.

When process and/or method development is required to provide the information required for a technology transfer package, steps in a technology transfer process are often performed in parallel to facilitate the knowledge transfer and overall timing of the transfer. In this third case study, intermediate scale pilot batches were performed to ensure the ability to scale-up the process and to prove the control strategy for the CPPs.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

五階段技術轉移流程 (Five-Stage TT Process)：本指南針對小分子 API 轉移提出的改良版流程，與第 3 章的六階段流程相比，將重點放在跨功能協作與定期風險審查。每個階段設有指導委員會 (Steering Committee) 的檢查點，必須通過評估才能進入下一階段。

ICH Q10 產品生命週期：製藥品質系統的基礎框架，技術轉移是其中的重要活動，必須在整個產品生命週期中系統性地管理知識。

重點提示：風險矩陣解讀 Risk Matrix Analysis

Table 10.1 揭示了一個重要規律：大於10倍放大（>10x Scale-up）永遠是高風險，無論是同廠還是異廠、新產品還是舊產品。這是因為：

  • 傳質/傳熱效果在大規模設備中行為不同
  • 混合時間、剪切力、冷卻/加熱速率都隨規模改變
  • CPP 的操作視窗可能在放大後收窄

反之，在同一廠點、同一生產線轉移低風險產品（無設備變更），風險可以降至 Low——但仍需 QMS 和方法轉移確認。

比喻說明 Analogy

五階段流程配備指導委員會的檢查點，就像蓋高樓時每完成一層必須通過結構安全檢驗才能繼續往上蓋。這種「停-驗-繼續」的節奏雖然看似減慢進度，實際上是在防止後期發現地基問題時的災難性返工成本。技術轉移的早期可行性評估就是「地基安全驗收」。

實務應用 CDMO Application

CDMO 的技術轉移模型（案例三，Figure 10.2）有一個關鍵特點：開發與轉移並行進行。這在 CDMO 環境中很常見，因為客戶往往希望在開發完成前就開始商業化準備。

實際執行原則：使用實驗室規模重現性批次來模擬植物規模的條件和停置時間，作為放大前的橋樑數據。這些批次同時確認 CPP 的控制策略，為後續中試批次提供依據。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼即使放大設備與送出廠完全相同，大於10倍的規模放大仍被評為高風險？
  2. 在 CDMO 環境中，開發與轉移並行的模式有何優點與潛在陷阱？
10.4 Technology Transfer Case Studies — 技術轉移案例研究

原文內容 Original Text

The first two case studies address the challenges associated with the potential technical, cultural, and organizational gaps between the sending and receiving units.

  • The first case study identified technology gaps driven by global differences in interpretation of CPPs and how they are controlled.
  • The second case study discusses differences in the interpretation of the global QMS.

Each of these small molecule API technology transfers were for a large, global pharmaceutical company where the sending and receiving units were internal to the same company, demonstrating that these challenges are not unique to external manufacture.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

重點提示 Key Notes

本節最重要的聲明：「這些挑戰不只存在於外部委外製造」。同一家大型跨國藥廠的兩個內部廠區在 CPP 解讀和 QMS 執行上仍然存在顯著差異。這說明問題的根源不是外部 vs 內部，而是知識的情境性（tacit knowledge）——許多關鍵操作知識藏在人腦中，而非文件裡。

10.4.1 Small Molecule Case Study #1: Supply Chain Driven Technology Transfer — 供應鏈驅動技術轉移

原文內容 Original Text

This case study is for a commercial-commercial transfer of an API that was already being commercially manufactured in Europe and imported for sale to the US market. Changes in importation regulations on the API and a portion of its raw materials were going to impact the ability to serve the US market. These changes created the business need to transfer commercial manufacture to the US within 3–6 months in order to maintain continuity of supply.

It was assumed the timing could be achieved for the following reasons:

  • API was produced commercially at a site internal to the company with well-established process criticality and control strategy
  • API had regulatory approval in the US
  • Initial plant scale would be smaller than the current equipment
  • The US-based development team was already working on a next generation process and analytical methods were already being used

At the kickoff meeting, the full cross-functional team was provided the technology transfer charter with the goals and boundaries of the transfer. Due to the condensed timeframe, a full risk assessment could not be performed until after the knowledge transfer had begun. The risk assessment identified key challenges in the initial assumptions as summarized in Table 10.2.

Table 10.2: Small Molecule Case Study #1 – Risk Assessment Challenges and Resolutions
Challenge Resolution
Clear understanding of process CPPs and control strategy was challenging due to local operational knowledge and a language barrier Face-to-face meetings between process and analytical team members. Involvement of operations personnel from the sending unit during process validation at the receiving unit.
Key analytical methods for in-process tests were not yet validated/qualified (focus had been on next generation process) Gaps identified early; receiving unit initiated co-validation between both units in time for process validation.
New equipment was a multi-purpose small volume production line that required design modifications specific to this API process Well-defined process allowed engineering to order long lead items shortly after kickoff. Equipment qualification remained on schedule.
Not all equipment between sites was equivalent, impacting the regulatory strategy for site approval Additional development studies performed to provide data supporting product equivalence with available equipment.
Installation of new milling suite: despite identical milling equipment, problems in obtaining particle size distribution specification Plant scale milling trials performed to identify milling process parameters achieving PSD specification.

Challenge: CPP Knowledge Transfer

Although the technology transfer was between two internal company sites, access to operations information and data was limited. Review of historical manufacturing batch records, validation reports, and CPPs identified significant gaps:

  • Accurate translation of batch records to English impacted ability to understand local operational practices
  • Philosophy in the identification and control of CPPs
  • Process data availability
"pH was to be controlled tightly in a specified range as measured using an in-process control sample. However, information such as the location of the sample, how the measurement was obtained and validated, and accuracy of the data was not well understood based on the technology transfer information provided."

Another example was interpretation of the allowed flowrate of a reactant into the reactor. The documented criticality justification stated that the flowrate was a critical parameter to be maintained between 0.5–1.0 liters/min. However, the batch records appeared to measure only the total time rather than a rate across the entire reactant charge — a common practice at the sending unit which differed slightly from the criticality justification.

Learning

Face-to-face meetings with the sending unit cross-functional team allowed the receiving unit to obtain the required process information. A crucial element was the involvement of the technicians with expertise performing the actual batch operations. These interactions developed a stronger relationship between sites, facilitating remote cooperation throughout the transfer. Technicians/operators and engineers from the sending unit participated at the receiving unit during the manufacture of process validation batches.

Outcome

Successful process validation was performed at the receiving unit three months after the start of the technology transfer, allowing the receiving unit to be filed as a manufacturer with no gap in API supply for the US market.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Commercial-to-Commercial Transfer (商業→商業轉移)：送出廠和接收廠都是 GMP 商業製造場地，API 已有法規批准。這類轉移理論上風險較低，但本案例顯示法規變化（進口限制）可以突然創造3-6個月的壓縮時程，迫使團隊在知識轉移完整性與速度之間妥協。

Technology Transfer Charter (技術轉移章程)：定義轉移目標、範圍、邊界、責任人的正式文件，是技術轉移的「合約」，必須在啟動會議時讓所有跨功能成員理解並承諾。

重點提示：隱性知識陷阱 Tacit Knowledge Gap

本案例的核心教訓在於文件記錄的 CPP 與實際操作之間的落差：

  • 批記錄上記載的是「流速 0.5-1.0 L/min」，但實際操作是量測「總加料時間」
  • pH 管控的取樣位置、量測方式未在文件中清楚說明

這種落差在語言障礙加持下更難發現。結論：批記錄本身不足以轉移製程知識，操作人員的親身參與不可替代。

重點提示：磨粉設備等效的陷阱 Milling Equivalence Trap

「設備相同 = 製程相同」是技術轉移中最危險的假設之一。本案例中，接收廠安裝了與送出廠完全相同型號的磨粉設備，仍然無法達到粒徑分佈規格，最終需要額外的工廠規模磨粉試驗才能找到正確的製程參數。原因可能包括：環境濕度差異、進料方式不同、磨盤磨損程度等細節因素。

比喻說明 Analogy

CPP 知識轉移就像請廚師把一道菜的食譜交給新廚師。食譜上寫「中火翻炒3分鐘」，但原廚師知道這是在使用特定型號的爐具——新廚師的爐火可能大兩倍，3分鐘就焦了。批記錄就是食譜，但真正的知識藏在廚師腦中。讓原廚師親臨現場教學（technician on-site），才是解決方案。

案例成果指標 Case Outcome Metrics

時程壓力：3-6 個月完成商業→商業轉移
實際完成：從轉移啟動到製程驗證完成 = 3 個月
成果：無斷供風險，按時向 FDA 申報新製造廠

關鍵成功因素：
+ 早期識別方法驗證缺口 → 即時啟動共同驗證
+ 長交期設備（Long Lead Items）於 Kickoff 後立即採購
+ 技術人員親臨接收廠參與製程驗證批次

實務應用 CDMO Application

身為 CDMO 接收端，當客戶提出「3-6 個月完成轉移」的壓縮時程要求時，本案例提供了一個重要的操作框架：

  • 立即執行：方法缺口評估 + 長交期設備識別（Day 1 Kickoff 之後）
  • 安排技術人員互訪：讓客戶操作人員到 CDMO 廠參與首批或驗證批
  • 語言管理：如果客戶文件是非英文，要求提供官方英文翻譯，並由雙方技術人員確認操作實務
  • 設備等效性評估：即使設備型號相同，也要進行製程參數確認試驗

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 如果你是接收廠的技術轉移負責人，在 Kickoff 會議後的第一週你最優先做的三件事是什麼？
  2. 「文件記載的 CPP 操作方式」與「實際批次操作方式」之間的落差，如何在轉移前系統性地識別出來？
  3. 本案例中，為何即使送出廠和接收廠在同一公司，仍出現了語言障礙？這對跨國 CDMO 合作有何啟示？
10.4.2 Small Molecule Case Study #2: Alignment of Quality Management Requirements for Method Transfer — 分析方法轉移的 QMS 對齊

原文內容 Original Text

This case study is for a development-commercial transfer of a set of related APIs being developed in Europe for commercial manufacture in the US. While these APIs were new to the company's portfolio, they were already commercially available in the US using a different process route. Each API already had CQAs developed and filed with the drug product manufacturers.

The development and technology transfer teams were internal to a large, global pharmaceutical company, following the same global QMS guidelines. The sending unit (development team) was responsible for designing all aspects of the process including analytical method development. Program management of the technology transfer was performed at the receiving unit with cross-functional members having oversight in the ongoing development activities.

The technology transfer of each API was to be performed sequentially under tight timelines to achieve contract deadlines with the drug product manufacturer. However, development of each API process was being performed in parallel with analytical methods that significantly overlapped the APIs.

Challenge

While both development and manufacturing were at internal locations, interpretation of the global QMS for analytical method transfer, qualification, and validation requirements differed locally between Europe and the US. This was going to cause excessive redundant analysis and documentation activities.

For compendial methods, the global policy required the method to be confirmed by running on a reference sample. The sending unit used material generated in development laboratory batches. The receiving unit required a method qualification involving testing using a qualified reference standard. In summary, global policy required validation of non-compendial methods but local differences were found in:

  • Testing requirements for the sending and receiving laboratories performing the validation
  • Documentation requirements

Learning

The project team worked with the drug product manufacturer, internal business team, and quality/regulatory to establish boundaries for the method development work:

  • CQAs and limits already filed by the drug product manufacturer were to align where possible
  • Drug product manufacturer analytical methods would be used where applicable and if not proprietary
  • New impurities formed from the new process would be identified if greater than 0.10%

The development and technology transfer project managers facilitated negotiations over a six-month period between the local quality groups. A blend of approaches (shown in Tables 10.3 and 10.4) was implemented to satisfy the key desired QMS elements yet reduce the required amount of sample materials, testing time, and number of resources.

"The receiving laboratory acted as the second laboratory verification required for completion of the method validation with both laboratories using the same sample; this approach reduced the time for method validation in half."

Prior to any analytical work, an agreement was signed between the sending and receiving units establishing criteria for all analytical work associated with these technology transfers — boundaries establishing the workflow for all analysts developing and transferring the methods.

Outcome

The negotiated approach was formally documented. Alignment of the QMS significantly reduced costs and allowed proper definition of required resources. The blended approach allowed 21 methods to become verifications/qualifications rather than validations, resulting in a time savings of over a year for one analyst. In total:

  • 80 method verifications/qualifications
  • 8 full method validations

Additionally, a system was agreed upon allowing multiple verifications and products to be combined into fewer documents. This system was adopted internally for future technology transfers.

Impurities HPLC 3 2 APIs
